## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of state (x, v) and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form for (non)linear harmonic oscillators. Common models include linear damping/restoring forces and nonlinear stiffness, nonlinear damping, and external/parametric forcing terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (undamped) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (restoring acceleration proportional to displacement; sign absorbed in c0)
- Linear viscous damping + spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (mass-normalized spring + damping; c1 typically negative)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven with phase shift: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (equivalent forcing representation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity plus damping)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like damping proportional to speed squared)
- Nonlinear stiffness (odd polynomial): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (higher-order conservative nonlinearity)
- Simple pendulum small-to-large angle model: dv_dt = c0 * sin(x) + c1 * v (nonlinear restoring force from geometry plus damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v + c3 * x (state-dependent damping; signs absorbed in constants)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear damping creating limit cycles)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness / parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (canonical nonlinear forced oscillator)
- Nonlinear coupling of stiffness and damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + (c2 + c3 * x**2) * v (amplitude-dependent damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative oscillator signature: dv_dt depends primarily on x (and odd functions of x like x, x**3, sin(x)) with minimal explicit t dependence; implies an underlying potential energy.
- Viscous dissipation: a term linear in v (c * v) indicates damping proportional to velocity; typically reduces amplitude without changing equilibrium position.
- Aerodynamic/impact-like losses: v * Abs(v) (or other even-in-v factors times v) indicates drag scaling with speed squared and stronger damping at high speeds.
- Hardening/softening stiffness: inclusion of x**3 (or higher odd powers) shifts the effective oscillation frequency with amplitude (backbone curve behavior).
- Geometric nonlinearity: sin(x) (or truncated series x - c*x**3) suggests pendulum/rotational restoring forces rather than linear springs.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles: state-dependent damping like (c0 + c1 * x**2) * v (van der Pol-type) can inject energy at small amplitudes and dissipate at large amplitudes.
- Nonlinear damping-generated cycles: odd powers in v (e.g., v**3) can produce amplitude-limited oscillations even with linear stiffness.
- External periodic forcing: additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms produce resonance peaks and steady-state oscillations at the drive frequency.
- Parametric resonance: multiplicative modulation (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x indicates time-varying stiffness; instability bands occur near specific frequency ratios.

\[
(-0.431673711555058)\,v\;+\;(0.431673711555058)\,v x^2\;+\;(-1.47162300874852)\,x^3\;+\;(-1.47162300874852)\,x\;+\;(-1.47162300874852\cdot 0.0306959168053925)\,t x

- \(v x^2\): \(+0.431673711555058\)
- \(x^3\): \(-1.47162300874852\)
- \(x\): \(-1.47162300874852\)

1) Has extra terms \(v(c5+x)^2\), rational-in-\(v\) terms. To match GT globally, must set those coefficients to 0: \(c4=c6=c9=0\). Then it reduces to linear combo of \(x,x^3,v,tx\) only, but it lacks the \(v x^2\) term unless it comes from \(c4 v(c5+x)^2\), which we just killed. If we keep \(c4\neq 0\), \(v(c5+x)^2 = v(x^2+2c5 x+c5^2)\) introduces unwanted \(v x\) and \(v\) offsets unless \(c5=0\). With \(c5=0\), it becomes \(c4 v x^2\) only (good). 2) Contains \(v(c8+x)^2\) (can generate \(v x^2\) if \(c8=0\)) but also has rational-in-\(x\) terms \(c4*x/(c5*x+c6)\) and \(c9/(c5*x+c6)\). To avoid non-polynomial dependence, need \(c4=c9=0\). Then use \(c7 v(x+c8)^2\) with \(c8=0\) to get \(v x^2\). Works. ✅

3) Has \(v(c5+x)^2\) (good if \(c5=0\)) but also has \(x/(c7 v+c8)\) and \(1/(c7 v+c8)\) terms; must set \(c6=c9=0\) to remove them. Then it’s like (1) and can match. ✅
